  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e521549d-d4ed-4f6a-a282-e266bfd6f525'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText15909190448130702187" style="display:none">Greg Gaines is the last master of high school espionage, able to disappear at will into any social environment. He has only one friend, Earl, and together they spend their time making movies, their own incomprehensible versions of Coppola and Herzog cult classics.<br /><br />Until Greg’s mother forces him to rekindle his childhood friendship with Rachel.<br /><br />Rachel has been diagnosed with leukemia—-cue extreme adolescent awkwardness—-but a parental mandate has been issued and must be obeyed. When Rachel stops treatment, Greg and Earl decide the thing to do is to make a film for her, which turns into the Worst Film Ever Made and becomes a turning point in each of their lives.<br /><br />And all at once Greg must abandon invisibility and stand in the spotlight.</span>

<div id="review_329859027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/329859027" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/329859027?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer329859027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11162487728613573545"><blockquote>
  <i>“If after reading this book you come to my home and brutally murder me, I do not blame you.” </i>
</blockquote><br/>I know this is an awful thing to say, but I am so tired of all the "illness romance" books we've seen since <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars' title='The Fault in Our Stars by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Fault in Our Stars</a>. They're so hung up on leaving the reader with a beautiful message about life and/or death, so intent on making you cry and showing how a person can gain a new outlook or fall in love from being close to someone with a terminal illness. <br/><br/>In real life, <b>very few people are l</b></span>
  <span id="freeText11162487728613573545" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“If after reading this book you come to my home and brutally murder me, I do not blame you.” </i>
</blockquote><br />I know this is an awful thing to say, but I am so tired of all the "illness romance" books we've seen since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a>. They're so hung up on leaving the reader with a beautiful message about life and/or death, so intent on making you cry and showing how a person can gain a new outlook or fall in love from being close to someone with a terminal illness. <br /><br />In real life, <b>very few people are lucky enough to take something amazing away from an experience like that</b>. Andrews knows it, and he does such a great job of delivering a book that is hilarious with colourful characters, that contains a girl with cancer, but doesn't strain itself to give us a life lesson.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Look, I was an idiot. I didn't want people to think that I had a crush, so I decided to give everyone the impression that I truly, honestly hated Madison Harter. For no reason. Just thinking about this makes me want to punch myself in the eyeball.” </i>
</blockquote><br />One of the best things about this book is that the illness is a subplot in an otherwise really funny novel. <b>This is the most I've laughed at a story in a very long time</b>. Greg is a fantastic protagonist and the jokes vary between witty sarcasm and a bit of ridiculous schoolboy humour - who knew breasts could be such a source of hilarity? And the even better thing is that Andrews doesn't try to manipulate the reader's emotions, I didn't feel like I was being forced to cry or pity Rachel, and I appreciated the author's message that sometimes shit happens, things go wrong and people die, and we don't necessarily learn anything useful from it, other than the fact that shit happens, things go wrong and people die.<br /><br />Greg feels like he should be moved by Rachel's illness, he feels like he should hang out with her, and yet Andrews allows him to acknowledge that he isn't moved, he doesn't really want to help out or get involved, in fact he finds himself wishing he could ignore the whole situation, carry on with his life, and pretend it isn't happening. Maybe you won't like this sentiment, but <b>it felt a million times more honest and real than any other book about illness that I can remember</b>.<br /><br />I think that what I like about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12700353.Me_and_Earl_and_the_Dying_Girl" title="Me and Earl and the Dying Girl by Jesse Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Me and Earl and the Dying Girl</a> is what's lacking in Green's work. Andrews' characters are not life lessons, not philosophers, not poets, they're just kids in the worst kind of situation. And they're also incredibly funny.<br /><br />If you're looking for a honest and hilarious story with a great cast of characters, I'm pretty confident <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12700353.Me_and_Earl_and_the_Dying_Girl" title="Me and Earl and the Dying Girl by Jesse Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Me and Earl and the Dying Girl</a> is for you.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11162487728613573545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2492942462" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2492942462" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2492942462?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781419719608" href="/book/show/25110515-me-and-earl-and-the-dying-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2492942462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9312145821199127797"><blockquote>
  <i>If after reading this book you come to my home and brutally murder me, I do not blame you.</i>
</blockquote>Greg Gaines survived (most of) high school by following his flawless system of <b>staying at the periphery </b>- be nice but not<b>
  <i> too</i>
</b> nice. Laugh but not <b>
  <i>too</i>
</b> loud. Exist...but only enough for people to<b>
  <i> barely</i>
</b> notice. <br/><br/>He has his meritocracy, his long-time friend (Earl) and his quirky collection of homemade movies (made with Earl) - he's all ready to<b> survive, graduate and move on.</b><br/><br/>But then his mom deci</span>
  <span id="freeText9312145821199127797" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>If after reading this book you come to my home and brutally murder me, I do not blame you.</i>
</blockquote>Greg Gaines survived (most of) high school by following his flawless system of <b>staying at the periphery </b>- be nice but not<b>
  <i> too</i>
</b> nice. Laugh but not <b>
  <i>too</i>
</b> loud. Exist...but only enough for people to<b>
  <i> barely</i>
</b> notice. <br /><br />He has his meritocracy, his long-time friend (Earl) and his quirky collection of homemade movies (made with Earl) - he's all ready to<b> survive, graduate and move on.</b><br /><br />But then his mom decides to throw <b>one huge wrench</b> in his great aims of blending into the background - <b>
  <i>by forcing him to be friends with the cancer-girl.</i>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>Mom was asking me to resume a friendship that had no honest foundation and ended on screamingly awkward terms. How do you do that? You can’t.</i>
</blockquote>And...with much <b>grumbling and prodding and outright threatening,</b> he agrees. <br /><br />And his whole plan - the mediocrity, the movies, the periphery - <b> crumbles into dust. </b><blockquote>
  <i>There was just something about her dying that I had understood but not really understood..you can know someone is dying on an intellectual level, but emotionally it hasn't really hit you, and then when it does, that's when you feel like shit.</i>
</blockquote> <b>Wow - like <i>seriously,</i> wow. </b><br /><br />This one surprised me. <br /><br />Greg's story is certainly not a typical-teen-cancer sort of book. <blockquote>
  <i>So if this were a normal book about a girl with leukemia, I would probably talk a shitload about all the meaningful things Rachel had to say as she got sicker and sicker, and also probably we would fall in love and have some incredibly fulfilling romantic thing and she would die in my arms. But I don't feel like lying to you. She didn't have meaningful things to say, and we definitely didn't fall in love.</i>
</blockquote>Jesse Andrew's novel simply <b>felt more real </b>than all of those other ones I've read.<br /><br />It didn't dance around the topic,<b> it didn't tug at your heartstrings </b>in just the right way, and there was no chaste-fade-to-black sex scene. <br /><br />There are so many<b> beautiful-cancer-books</b> out there that this one was truly a relief. <br /><br /><b>This book was funny, crass, rude and above all,<i> absolutely</i> real.</b> And for that, I truly appreciate this novel.<br /><br />There were times where I wanted to shake Greg, shake Rachel, shake Greg and Rachel at the same time...and (above all) wrap Earl in a huge hug. <br /><br />Definitely one to read!<blockquote>
  <i>But you gotta live your own life. You gotta take care a your own shit before you get started doing things for errybody else.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9312145821199127797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_666952652" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/666952652" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20648313-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435035988p2/20648313.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/666952652?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/20648313-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20648313-emma?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20648313-emma?shelf=summer-reads-2013">summer-reads-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20648313-emma?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20648313-emma?shelf=beautiful-covers">beautiful-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20648313-emma?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20648313-emma?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20648313-emma?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20648313-emma?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer666952652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12775964475498515306">Umm… I don't know exactly what to say about this book. It seems to me like one of those cult books where if you love it, you love it, but if you don't, you don't. There were parts of it that were funny, but the majority of the parts that I felt were meant to be funny just fell flat. The cover is absolutely beautiful and there were some parts that I definitely enjoyed… but, it just didn't do it for me. <br/><br/>This book is about Greg and Earl and Rachel. Greg is a high school senior and he and Earl are a</span>
  <span id="freeText12775964475498515306" style="display:none">Umm… I don't know exactly what to say about this book. It seems to me like one of those cult books where if you love it, you love it, but if you don't, you don't. There were parts of it that were funny, but the majority of the parts that I felt were meant to be funny just fell flat. The cover is absolutely beautiful and there were some parts that I definitely enjoyed… but, it just didn't do it for me. <br /><br />This book is about Greg and Earl and Rachel. Greg is a high school senior and he and Earl are amateur film makers (spoiler alert: They're not very good.) Rachel is Greg's old kind of girlfriend who recently became diagnosed with leukemia and is dying. There were some parts of this book were laugh-out-loud funny, but the non-funny bits and the kind of useless annoying bits made it a one star for me.<br /><br />SPOILER DISCUSSION<br /><br />Can I just talk about how much I hated all the "this is such a bad book I don't even know why I'm writing this I'm going to throw the laptop if you're enjoying this you should punch your own eye" parts. Why? I don't know if it was kind of supposed to be funny and enjoyable and like, "haha, he's making fun of himself" but it came across like those people who are always talking about how ugly they are and you just want them to shut up!<br /><br />Let's just spend a second talking about this cover. So gorgeous. I'm so in love with it. All the art was amazing, it was just the story… blah.<br /><br />I liked all the alternate ways of telling the stories. Bullet points and script format and all of that. Probably my favorite part of the whole rading experience.<br /><br />I honestly didn't care about the characters at all. And I think that's the issue, even when Rachel died I was like, "eh, what a shame." Greg seemed like a total jerk, I could get used to Earl in a way and I actually enjoyed his character, but it was just odd.<br /><br />Another thing about this book, it felt like it was trying so hard to be eccentric and different. Like how there were all the dorky goth kids and Mr. Mcarthy and all of Earl's brothers. Not everyone is eccentric like that. For a lot of people, you have to get to know them and then you figure out all their little quirks. There is no place that I'm aware of where you can have teachers who are shoeless in class and kids who beat up on each other randomly and a girl dying of cancer and a kid so unable to feel things and only able to beat up on himself but who likes to make films anyway so his future self can just talk about how much they suck some more. That is just too much in my opinion. There have to be some "normal" people.<br /><br />I liked some of the plot, but so much of it was tangents and they didn't really make sense to me and we didn't really get to know any of the characters (I'm sure there was some deep stuff going on that I just didn't catch onto, and really we know that Earl has spent so much time trying to help his mother and all that,) but it just isn't anywhere near enough for me.<br /><br />END!<br /><br />Somewhat amusing, not at all sad, weird book: 53%</span>
  <a data-text-id="12775964475498515306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1662046581" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1662046581" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1662046581?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=cancer">cancer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1662046581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10390816127660880800">It’s rare for me not to know what to say about a book. And I guess I do know what to say about this one, but my thoughts are very different from other people, so just keep in mind that we all perceive things, characters, scenes, etc. differently.<br/><br/>Greg is a liar.<br/><br/>A big, fat liar, he would correct me.<br/><br/>From the beginning, he is lying to us. He says that his meeting Rachel who suffers from leukemia didn’t change anything inside him. He says he didn’t learn anything from this experience he lived and tha</span>
  <span id="freeText10390816127660880800" style="display:none">It’s rare for me not to know what to say about a book. And I guess I do know what to say about this one, but my thoughts are very different from other people, so just keep in mind that we all perceive things, characters, scenes, etc. differently.<br /><br />Greg is a liar.<br /><br />A big, fat liar, he would correct me.<br /><br />From the beginning, he is lying to us. He says that his meeting Rachel who suffers from leukemia didn’t change anything inside him. He says he didn’t learn anything from this experience he lived and that in no way has it changed his way of looking at things – cancer, death, friendship, life, etc.<br /><br />He even says it: <em>I learned absolutely nothing from Rachel’s leukemia.</em><br /><br /><em> </em>But those are lies. He’s so in denial it made me furious.<br /><br />He’s not in touch with his emotions. He’s the type of person who wants to steer clear of altercations at all cost. To make his life simpler, he even decides to befriend everyone at school, without really befriending them, so he could steer clear of any drama befalling him, too.<br /><br />Now I liked him. I really did. I thought he was adorably goofy and awkward. He doesn’t share my type of humour, but that doesn’t mean I didn’t find this book entertaining.<br /><br />It <em>is</em>. I was always a huge fan of ‘‘special novels’’ I like to call them. The ones that defy the idea of what a novel should consist of. The ones that aren’t always written in paragraphs and very often use book-related props: letters, bullet points, various fonts, etc.<br /><br />I liked its original narration and Greg himself. Though I couldn’t agree with him all the time and I still don’t, he’s a kid a small part of me could connect with.<br /><br />The part that doesn’t know where it belongs in this life. What to study? What school to choose? Where to go and what to do? He and I are very different people and we probably would never be friends, but I can say that he’s a good kid.<br /><br />Most of the dialogs make sense – thank god – and the humour in form of figures of speech is not hard to decrypt and even the writing is somewhat enjoyable.<br /><br />BUT THE PLOT, or rather the lack of it, may get on your nerves. The book is fairly fast-paced and interestingly put together (with all of them book-related props) to not lose interest in it, but it does leave the reader thinking, ‘‘Is that it, motherfucker?’’<br /><br />Yup, that’s it.<br /><br />I wish you all the best, Greg.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10390816127660880800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText15287430929166747919" style="display:none">The humor was crude just for the sake of being crude and I didn't laugh once. <div id="review_354378889" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/354378889" />
    <a title="Teresa Bunner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3973542-teresa-bunner"><img alt="Teresa Bunner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1284491504p2/3973542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/354378889?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Teresa Bunner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Teresa Bunner" href="/user/show/3973542-teresa-bunner">Teresa Bunner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer354378889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer78788587001335304">I can appreciate snarky. And snarky certainly describes our narrator. The problem is, I can appreciate snarky when I like the character. I never grew to like Greg. And because I didn't like him or the story line, things like the excessive cussing in the book really bothered me. Had I liked or felt drawn to the characters, I could forgive that flaw. Heaven knows I can speak in language that would make my mother cringe and a sailor seem tame.<br/><br/>I was so excited to find a book with an African American</span>
  <span id="freeText78788587001335304" style="display:none">I can appreciate snarky. And snarky certainly describes our narrator. The problem is, I can appreciate snarky when I like the character. I never grew to like Greg. And because I didn't like him or the story line, things like the excessive cussing in the book really bothered me. Had I liked or felt drawn to the characters, I could forgive that flaw. Heaven knows I can speak in language that would make my mother cringe and a sailor seem tame.<br /><br />I was so excited to find a book with an African American character represented on the front cover. And then I was appalled as Earl and his family were defined in painful stereotypes of the African American community. Single mom, stepdad left, multiple boyfriends, alcoholic. Brothers who are "gangbangers" and sell drugs, a run-down house. Earl is described as looking perpetually "pissed" and having anger issues and violent tendencies. At the end, he goes to work at Wendy's instead of pursuing college.<br /><br />Greg, on the other hand, is white, lives with both parents, father is a college professor, mom runs a non-profit. 2 sisters who, as far as we know, are good kids. Pursues film school at the behest of the dying girl.<br /><br />I think it really got to me when Greg described the school principal "an African American guy", big and scary and with the same "pissed" look that Earl has. Now the author has created two "angry" African American males.<br /><br />I know there are those who will argue that they know someone like Earl, that it is "reality", that I am too sensitive. But these descriptors are not accidents. If we are going to put books in the hands of kids, then we have to begin to be willing to have the hard conversations that ask why the reality here is so starkly different for these two characters. Why can't the race of the two characters be switched? Are we going to perpetually defend the use of these stereotypes? I just can't. </span>
  <a data-text-id="78788587001335304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_801353327" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/801353327" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/801353327?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who think they can't read or enjoy &quot;cancer books&quot;</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Steph by: </span>
      Raeleen Lemay
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=tough-issues">tough-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=amulet">amulet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=best-characters">best-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-own-it">i-own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2014-favs">2014-favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2012-release">2012-release</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer801353327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17047261064446621832">This is the book I wish received more attention than <em>The Fault in Our Stars</em>. Unlike the aforementioned novel, it doesn't glamorize a terminal illness and try in any way to make light of the situation. In case that offends anyone, keep in mind that <a title='Review: The Fault in Our Stars by John Green' href='http://cuddlebuggery.com/blog/2013/08/08/review-the-fault-in-our-stars-by-john-green/' rel='nofollow noopener'>I did enjoy TFIOS</a>, but I just think<em> Me, Earl and the Dying Girl</em> had a more powerful message.<br/><br/>This isn't going to be a book for everyone. The protagonist is an anti-hero who will anger the reader and make you wish he were a real person just so you could </span>
  <span id="freeText17047261064446621832" style="display:none">This is the book I wish received more attention than <em>The Fault in Our Stars</em>. Unlike the aforementioned novel, it doesn't glamorize a terminal illness and try in any way to make light of the situation. In case that offends anyone, keep in mind that <a title="Review: The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/blog/2013/08/08/review-the-fault-in-our-stars-by-john-green/" rel="nofollow noopener">I did enjoy TFIOS</a>, but I just think<em> Me, Earl and the Dying Girl</em> had a more powerful message.<br /><br />This isn't going to be a book for everyone. The protagonist is an anti-hero who will anger the reader and make you wish he were a real person just so you could slap some sense into him. He is flawed in every possible way, but he was so realistic, that I couldn't help but to kinda like him. Maybe. In a strange turn of events, Greg finds himself hanging out with Rachel, a girl in his class that was recently diagnosed with cancer. And he hates it. In the beginning he feels a sense of obligation to spend time with her because she's dying. He gets that she's dying, but he doesn't understand how to handle it, and as a result, says some pretty offensive stuff to her and is just a general jerk. But he keeps trying to do better, visits her in the hospital and tries very hard to make her laugh until her last day.<br /><blockquote>“There was just something about her dying that I had understood but not <em>really </em>understood, if you know what I mean. I mean, you can know someone is dying on an intellectual level, but emotionally it hasn't really hit you, and then when it does, that's when you feel like shit.”</blockquote><br />Greg showed a lot of growth in the end from going from a character who didn't seem like he gave a shit to one who became obsessed with helping a friend, who didn't realize how much her dying was affecting him.<br /><blockquote>“And the point of Rachel the Film should really have been to express how awful and shitty that loss was, that she would have become a person with a long awesome life if she had been allowed to continue living, and that this was just a stupid meaningless loss, a motherfucking loss, a loss loss loss fucking loss, there was no fucking meaning to it, there was nothing that could come out of it...”</blockquote><br />What I loved the most was how <em>Me, Earl and the Dying Girl</em> showed a teen who didn't know how to deal with losing a friend, something I'm sure many teens don't understand. Death sucks. Seeing it happens just multiplies that times 1,000. There are no heroes in a story like that. I appreciate that Andrews showed that side.<br /><br />Also, bonus points for completely getting Earl's character and family right! POC that actually sound and act like POC!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17047261064446621832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Nothing much really happens--in terms of both plot or character development--and despite that, driven alone by the MC, Greg's, humorous voice, the book ends up being an awesome read.<br/><br/>Just to lay out how hilarious Greg's jokes ar</span>
  <span id="freeText9094733404083805577" style="display:none">This is me during, hmm, let's see, 90% of this book:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/410729.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I kid you not. This book made me laugh my ASS OFF. I have never in my whole life laughed this much while reading a book. Jesse Andrews, for this alone, YOU ARE AWESOME.<br><br>M&amp;E&amp;tDG is one of the weirdest books I've ever read. Nothing much really happens--in terms of both plot or character development--and despite that, driven alone by the MC, Greg's, humorous voice, the book ends up being an awesome read.<br><br>Just to lay out how hilarious Greg's jokes are, here's an excerpt--although keep in mind, it's MUCH funnier in context:<br><br><b>...it's just never a good idea to compliment a girl's boobs. I had to learn this the hard way. Also, it's somehow worse to draw attention to the fact that there are two boobs. I don't know why this is, but it's true. "You have nice boobs." Bad. "You have two nice boobs." Worse. "Two boobs? Perfect." F minus.</b><br><br>If somehow you couldn't tell, the humor in this book ain't exactly G-rated.<br><br>And seeing as how this is a book about 'cancer', it's the last thing you'd expect it to be. The gist of the story has Greg, a more-or-less typical senior, bumbling along through the torture that is high school, when his life changes once his mother forces him to befriend Rachel, a girl he once knew in Hebrew school who has leukemia.<br><br>Here's the no. 1 reason I loved this book: It proves that life does not have to be so fucking serious all the time. Right before M&amp;E&amp;tDG I read this very poignant novel about bipolar disorder, and it left me feeling utterly bereft, so saying that this book helped lighten my mood is saying quite a bit. Even though the book is about cancer, it doesn't force itself to be all falsely emotional and life-affirming etc etc. Because sometimes death isn't soul-crushing and earth-shattering and la-di-da--sometimes it just <i>is</i>, ya know? (Please tell me I did not sound like a soulless bastard when I said that.)<br><br>Greg's also obsessed with film making, and he loves this one movie so much--<i>Aguirre, Wrath of God</i>--that he convinced even me to watch to it. Even though (a) the movie is in German, (b) it's ages old, and (c) it's, well, old and foreign! So parts of the book include him making movies with Earl, his best friend, who's also a great source for laughs. Some of the novel is in script format, and parts of it are so hilarious I had cramps from laughing so hard.<br><br>I will admit, however, that sometimes Greg's jokes <i>did</i> get a tad tiring. There's only so much self-deprecation you can take before it gets annoying. Even so, his sense of humor is seriously out-of-the-park zany. Also, the last 40 pages for me, I dunno, fell a bit flat. Maybe I was expecting something even a tiny bit profound to finally happen, or maybe it was that Greg stopped cracking jokes every third sentence, which is sort of the strongest point of the book.<br><br>Who cares, though, really? Reading this book was an awwwesome, hysterically funny and upbeat experience, and if that's what you're looking for, definitely fetch a copy of this book for yourself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9094733404083805577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=lol">lol</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1255977223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17037458268382139889"><br/>Even though at the end of each chapter (and there are 40 chapters, plus an author's note and an epilogue), the narrator keeps nagging at the reader about how stupid this book is and how the reader will not learn anything, I on the contrary have an endless list to negate such claim.<br/><br/><b> All of these things and more are what I learned from the book: </b><br/><br/>1. If the author through his main character keeps warning you to stop reading his "stupid book", by all means read it. Even if he tells you that you might</span>
  <span id="freeText17037458268382139889" style="display:none"><br />Even though at the end of each chapter (and there are 40 chapters, plus an author's note and an epilogue), the narrator keeps nagging at the reader about how stupid this book is and how the reader will not learn anything, I on the contrary have an endless list to negate such claim.<br /><br /><b> All of these things and more are what I learned from the book: </b><br /><br />1. If the author through his main character keeps warning you to stop reading his "stupid book", by all means read it. Even if he tells you that you might want to commit homicide or murder the author himself after reading the book, <b> READ IT. </b> Because I can promise you that it is going to be one of the most original books you'll ever read.<br /><br />2. The book made me realize that Veronica Roth patterned the premise of her phenomenal series on the most mundane and most common institution- the High School. It's really no different from a post apocalyptic society with factions like the ff:<br /><br /> a. The Band Group- Amity<br /> b. The Theater Group-Abnegation <br /> c. The Smart Group- Erudite<br /> d. The Jocs- Candor<br /> e. The Stoners- Dauntless<br /> f. The loners- Factionless. <br /><br /> * Note: The classifications of high school factions are from the book. The analysis and the link to Divergent factions were done by yours truly.^^<br /><br />3. I'm not very good with acronyms and it's always a pleasure to learn a new one. I learned one from the book. <b> HGWAASGHPAWNIDYL </b> as in Hot Girls Who Are Also Sympathetic Good-Hearted People and Will Not Intentionally Destroy Your Life. LMAO!<br /><br />4. I learned a lot about film making. <br /><br />5. The general idea about how people look like rodents or birds.<br /><br />6. The excessive modesty reflex which is clearly annoying but it just can't be helped. <br /><br />7. Just because something is weird and hard to understand doesn't mean it's creative. Lol. This is HONESTLY true!<br /><br />8. The use of the phrase "little did I know" totally doesn't make sense and I was laughing so hard because I sometimes use this phrase in my reviews. That is definitely going to change from now on.^^<br /><br />9. Books about cancer don't always have to be terribly emotional and heartbreaking and that it's possible for a book to make me laugh out loud page after page. <br /><br />10. That for a book to be smart doesn't have to include extremely smart characters and sophisticated words. <br /></span>

<div id="review_1518695153" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1518695153" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1518695153?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/25609294-me-and-earl-and-the-dying-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2016-audios">2016-audios</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2016-ya-challenge">2016-ya-challenge</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1518695153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4279570467073388282"><b>4-4.5 stars</b> <br/><br/><i>Me and Earl and the Dying Girl</i>: YA book #3 for me in 2016. It was a really good pick! Thank you to my bestie for suggesting we do this one on audio together! So before I get into this review, lets chat for a minute. Anyone who knows me knows I collect signed books. I have hundreds. It’s a problem (not really… but) Anyways, I was in a different city in a bookstore with my husband and in-laws. I’m texting Beverly and she’s all “Chris- see if they have hardback copies of this book we’re</span>
  <span id="freeText4279570467073388282" style="display:none"><b>4-4.5 stars</b> <br><br><i>Me and Earl and the Dying Girl</i>: YA book #3 for me in 2016. It was a really good pick! Thank you to my bestie for suggesting we do this one on audio together! So before I get into this review, lets chat for a minute. Anyone who knows me knows I collect signed books. I have hundreds. It’s a problem (not really… but) Anyways, I was in a different city in a bookstore with my husband and in-laws. I’m texting Beverly and she’s all “Chris- see if they have hardback copies of this book we’re listening to.” So, I go to the YA and look for a hardback. Low and behold… TWO SIGNED COPIES are sitting on the shelf! It’s like it was meant to be! So now we both have a signed copy of this awesome book!<br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Mobile%20Uploads/67BAE179-7112-4B76-946B-D9D0B02FAB99_zpsnd54q9ac.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453815932i/17875521._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 67BAE179-7112-4B76-946B-D9D0B02FAB99_zpsnd54q9ac.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Mobile%20Uploads/24E89198-4249-4EBA-8CE8-3249E51131A5_zpswemgjiax.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453815932i/17875522._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 24E89198-4249-4EBA-8CE8-3249E51131A5_zpswemgjiax.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Moving on- <br><br>So <i>Me and Earl and the Dying Girl</i> how do I even explain or review this book? It was hilarious. I’m sure there were tons of lines and scenes where it was totally inappropriate of me to laugh at, but I found myself constantly cracking up. Greg and Earl were the best. I don’t even know where they came up with this stuff, but it was so funny. <br><br>This is not just a book about a dying girl. It’s not a super sad book that will make you cry a river (I may have shed a tear or two… but I cry over everything so I can’t be trusted). This is a book about a teen boy who’s not perfect, and who's growing up and coping with difficult things the best way he can with his life and situations happening. I enjoyed this book so much, I’m going to buy the movie this weekend… lets hope it’s good! <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“When you convert a good book to a film. stupid things happen” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i> <br></span>

<div id="review_274742189" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/274742189" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/274742189?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      Kirkus
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer274742189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18084638658692328526">As seen on <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/02/ya-review-me-and-earl-and-the-dying-girl-by-jesse-andrews.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Readventurer</a><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12700353.Me_and_Earl_and_the_Dying_Girl' title='Me and Earl and the Dying Girl by Jesse Andrews' rel='nofollow noopener'>Me and Earl and the Dying Girl</a> was my second "cancer book" in as many months. Although both <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5227163.Jesse_Andrews' title='Jesse Andrews' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jesse Andrews</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1406384.John_Green' title='John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>John Green</a> had the same intention - to write a story about cancer that was different from those other tearjerky novels, in my eyes, Andrews was much more successful at stepping away from melodrama and cliches of the genre than Green. Of course, Andrews does not (yet) have a publicity platform of Green's magnitude to promote his novel, so I am glad to be able to</span>
  <span id="freeText18084638658692328526" style="display:none">As seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/02/ya-review-me-and-earl-and-the-dying-girl-by-jesse-andrews.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12700353.Me_and_Earl_and_the_Dying_Girl" title="Me and Earl and the Dying Girl by Jesse Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Me and Earl and the Dying Girl</a> was my second "cancer book" in as many months. Although both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5227163.Jesse_Andrews" title="Jesse Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Jesse Andrews</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1406384.John_Green" title="John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">John Green</a> had the same intention - to write a story about cancer that was different from those other tearjerky novels, in my eyes, Andrews was much more successful at stepping away from melodrama and cliches of the genre than Green. Of course, Andrews does not (yet) have a publicity platform of Green's magnitude to promote his novel, so I am glad to be able to help him out a little, because, from my perspective, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12700353.Me_and_Earl_and_the_Dying_Girl" title="Me and Earl and the Dying Girl by Jesse Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Me and Earl and the Dying Girl</a> is a better, more honest, more real book than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a>.<br /><br />It is better mainly because it does not try to force you into feeling all the obvious things we are expected to feel reading stories about young, terminally ill characters. There is a certain compulsion to idealize cancer kids, lives ending so tragically early and all that. It is also pretty common to practically guilt you into feeling sorry for their specific predicament. But I like that Andrews allows his characters, even his hero, to be resentful and maybe indifferent towards or burdened by the illness, that his cancer-stricken patient is not an ever-so-wise, heroic saint, that there are maybe no life lessons to learn from such personal tragedies. Maybe having a dying girl in your life is just an event that will affect you in a major way, or maybe it will not and that would be okay, too.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12700353.Me_and_Earl_and_the_Dying_Girl" title="Me and Earl and the Dying Girl by Jesse Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Me and Earl and the Dying Girl</a> is not all about cancer though, in fact, the dying girl subplot plays only a relatively small part in Greg's story. It is more about Greg defining himself, stopping to play so safe, about bringing a little more focus onto his future and about understanding of who he is. The author might be a little coy repeating again and again in his narrative that there is no point to this novel, but there is one.<br /><br />Another good thing about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12700353.Me_and_Earl_and_the_Dying_Girl" title="Me and Earl and the Dying Girl by Jesse Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Me and Earl and the Dying Girl</a> is that it is very funny. The success of the book with a reader will depend a lot on what he/she finds funny though, because, admittedly, the novel is filled with jokes of the bathroom variety, you know, boogers, boobs and boners. But it was funny to me nevertheless.<br /><br />Great dialogue, self-deprecating humor (albeit occasionally too self-deprecating to be not annoying), vulgarity, wacky secondary characters, fresh (to me) approach to portraying cancer - I enjoyed it all and I hope you will too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18084638658692328526" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1272063698" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1272063698" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1272063698?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=hate-the-characters-hate-the-book">hate-the-characters-hate-the-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=pleasantly-surprised">pleasantly-surprised</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=laugh-out-loud-humor">laugh-out-loud-humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=protagonists-i-want-to-laser-face">protagonists-i-want-to-laser-face</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=he-s-so-bad-but-he-does-it-so-well">he-s-so-bad-but-he-does-it-so-well</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=great-but-not-quite-there-yet">great-but-not-quite-there-yet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=real-problems">real-problems</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1272063698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16720350088230639867"><b>EDIT 17/10/2016:</b> I am so horrendously late to the party, but the movie is awesome. It keeps the humor and self-aware nature of the novel and adds just a pinch of poignancy to make it feel worthwhile. Because the book doesn't take itself seriously enough and I love that about it, but I also love how the producers tweaked it for a more mainstream audience. They're both brilliant on their own. <br/><br/>Side mini-rant: How on earth did it gross less than The Fault in Our Stars? It's an outrage. <br/><br/><b>(Original rev</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16720350088230639867" style="display:none"><b>EDIT 17/10/2016:</b> I am so horrendously late to the party, but the movie is awesome. It keeps the humor and self-aware nature of the novel and adds just a pinch of poignancy to make it feel worthwhile. Because the book doesn't take itself seriously enough and I love that about it, but I also love how the producers tweaked it for a more mainstream audience. They're both brilliant on their own. <br><br>Side mini-rant: How on earth did it gross less than The Fault in Our Stars? It's an outrage. <br><br><b>(Original review)<br><br>3.5 stars</b><br><br>Nice Natalie: I don't even know why we're here. This book is pure snark. We <i>love snark</i>! <br><br>Cynical Natalie: Not if the characters are assholes. Greg is like the worse version of that kid from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/389627.Diary_of_a_Wimpy_Kid__Diary_of_a_Wimpy_Kid___1_" title="Diary of a Wimpy Kid (Diary of a Wimpy Kid, #1) by Jeff Kinney" rel="nofollow noopener">Diary of a Wimpy Kid</a>. He's selfish, inconsiderate, and an all-around jerk. <br><br>Nice Natalie: What do you expect, he's a teenage boy. That's what makes him real. <br><br>Cynical Natalie: Just because he's a teenage boy doesn't give him liberty to be a douche. He treats Rachel like a burden, which I grudgingly accept because it is sort of realistic. But even towards the end when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she was dying <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, all he thought about was how <i>he</i> didn't want her to die and it made <i>him</i> really sad.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438663561ra/15740349.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nice Natalie: Greg already warned us ahead of time this isn't the kind of book where he goes through Acceptance and receives some big epiphany about life or something. It's a refreshing change from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a>.<br><br>And he's funny! <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I entered Excessive Modesty Mode. Nothing is stupider and more ineffective than Excessive Modesty Mode. It is a mode in which you show that you’re modest by arguing with someone who is trying to compliment you. Essentially, you are going out of your way to try to convince someone that you’re a jerk.” <br><br><br>“And if a jock. God forbid, witnesses you hobnobbing with theater kids, he will immediately assume you are gay, and there is no force on earth greater than the fear jocks have homosexuals. None. It's like the Jewish fear of Nazis, except the complete opposite with regard to who is beating the crap out of whom. So I guess it's more like the Nazi fear of Jews.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>We haven't laughed this hard at a book in ages.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: You know what else is funny? The Big Bang Theory. We love it to pieces and ship Shamy obsessively, but that doesn't mean its jokes aren't sometimes sexist, racist, and borderline offensive. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438610459ra/15734305.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Greg makes some pretty sexist jokes, like saying fourteen-year-old girls are psychotic and their hobbies include not eating and yelling at parents. I was a fourteen-year-old girl once and I'll kick him right in his experimental-film-loving nuts.<br><br>Nice Natalie: He wasn't that pretentious. Even you were impressed by how the author made him so relatable, even though his hobby is really indie. And the different formats are cool.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Point taken. But Rachel, whom this book is supposed to revolve around, hardly has any personality.<br><br>Nice Natalie: That's because Greg never took the time to know her. It's part of his character and why he's realistic—<br><br>Cynical Natalie: —and there's zero plot. It's just a big flow of events.<br><br>Nice Natalie: Not exactly. According to literature class (Cynical Natalie: Here we go), the climax of a plot doesn't have to contain fighter jets or explosions, the MC simply has to come to a great realization. Greg realizes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he wants to go to film school, even though he acknowledges he might just end up at Wendy's someday. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It resembles real life.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Yeah, but we read fiction to <i>escape</i> real life.<br><br>Nice Natalie: You secretly love it. You throw fits whenever endings are too happy. Me and Earl and the Dying Girl is gritty and unapologetic.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Whatever. I'm not watching the movie. The trailer leads me to think they made it a lot more The Fault in Our Fucking Stars than the original text and God knows we've had enough of that shit.<br><br>To quote this very book:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“When you convert a good book to a film, stupid things happen” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Nice Natalie: Oh, come on. I'm sure it won't be that bad.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Hey, if we're going to tussle over the film, we're doing it off-screen. Come're...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438610459ra/15734307.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br>Other Nice Natalie/Cynical Natalie <s>brawls</s> reviews:<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/372646324" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars </a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/989706383" rel="nofollow noopener">A Girl Like You</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/915207283" rel="nofollow noopener">If I Stay</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/940598996" rel="nofollow noopener">Dreams of Gods &amp; Monsters</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/933780638" rel="nofollow noopener">The Martian</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/281202430" rel="nofollow noopener">Catching Fire</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1255504583" rel="nofollow noopener">All The Rage</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1277898365" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember In The Ashes</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1543869637" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter &amp; the Cursed Child</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1478432310" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hammer of Thor</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1478432316" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ship of the Dead</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1758536754" rel="nofollow noopener">Caraval</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1566259389" rel="nofollow noopener">Warcross</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_281487576" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/281487576" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/281487576?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jo by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer281487576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7165282333334859320"><b>
  <u>An exchange.</u>
</b><br/><br/>“I think I’m gonna go and read my book.”<br/>“Oh? Which book is it?”<br/>“Just this hilarious book about cancer.”<br/><br/>And you should’ve seen the glare I received. <br/><i>Icyyyy. </i><br/><br/>You see <i>that</i> is the problem I fear I’m going to have with this book. I want to run around wildly and throw this book at people and yell “READ IT!” and they’ll be like “Woah, Jo, what’s it about?! Tell me everything!”<br/>“IT’S AMAZING!!!!”<br/>“Is it, is it really?”<br/>“YES YES! WHY AREN’T YOU READING IT NOW?!”<br/>“WHY ARE WE TALKING IN CAPITAL</span>
  <span id="freeText7165282333334859320" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>An exchange.</u>
</b><br /><br />“I think I’m gonna go and read my book.”<br />“Oh? Which book is it?”<br />“Just this hilarious book about cancer.”<br /><br />And you should’ve seen the glare I received. <br /><i>Icyyyy. </i><br /><br />You see <i>that</i> is the problem I fear I’m going to have with this book. I want to run around wildly and throw this book at people and yell “READ IT!” and they’ll be like “Woah, Jo, what’s it about?! Tell me everything!”<br />“IT’S AMAZING!!!!”<br />“Is it, is it really?”<br />“YES YES! WHY AREN’T YOU READING IT NOW?!”<br />“WHY ARE WE TALKING IN CAPITAL LETTERS AND EXCESSIVE PUNCTUATION!?!??!!?!?”<br />“BECAUSE IT’S BRILLIANT.”<br />“But what’s it actually about?”<br />“Um… well, there’s this guy and he’s friends with this girl and… um, well… she kind of has cancer. Well, no, I guess there’s no kinda about it, she does have cancer.”<br />“Oh god, it’s one of those books, isn’t it?”<br /><br />NO!<br />It is <u>not </u><i>one of thos</i>e books. Yes it’s about someone who has cancer but it’s not a cancer book. <br />Are you still with me? <br />I’ll take that as a yes.<br />I often think that some writers think that if a book is about (or, in this case, features) a difficult subject then their readers must be crying all the way through the book to show that they have succeeded in handling it in an honest and realistic way.<br />Thankfully, Mr Andrews shows that this is not the case. <br /><br />Although, while I’ve been writing this I’ve realised that, in my trying to convince you this that this book isn’t about cancer, all I’ve done is talk about cancer.<br />So, one last time with feeling or… um...y’know… bold writing.<br /><br /><b>THIS BOOK ISN’T ABOUT CANCER.<br /></b><br />So seeing as I’ve just been chatting on about this book is <i>not</i> about, I should probably talk about what it actually <i>is</i> about, shouldn’t I?<br />This book, in a nutshell, is about a boy stumbling wildly through adolescence with the help of a brilliant and hilarious friend named Earl.<br />Except I don’t really mean help… because Earl doesn’t really <i>help</i> him as such. He just swears a lot and is gross and crude and is just generally brilliant at random intervals throughout this book. Throw in some fantastic Son of Rambow-eqsque scenes and you have one of the funniest and memorable double acts in young adult literature.<br /><br />I really loved Greg, both as a character and a narrator. He was fresh, original and definitely the kind of person I would want to punch in the arm on numerous occasions. Yeah, he wasn’t always likeable but what seventeen year old boy is? <br />I could chat on for a bit about all my favourite Greg moments but when I went back and looked at my notes I realised I’d pretty much highlighted everything for the first few chapters and then I gave up and just vowed to re-read it again. <br />This book had pretty much everything: lists, scripts, film reviews. I loved these different styles because they were hilarious, original and really added a lot to the book.<br /><br />The only quibble I had was that some jokes went on for a <i>smidgeon</i> too long and I realised I had no idea how we’d got to that bit and I was probably just laughing because I thought I should be. <br />Oh, except that I also wish there was more Earl. He should get his own book… and television series. I would watch that religiously and probably buy the box set.<br /><br />I loved how this book never set out to trick you and lull you into a false sense of security of laughter only to bombard you with sadness and a message at the end. It stated from the get go that this was a hilarious and ridiculous book and if you were looking for a message and/or meaning, it’s your own fault if you’re left disappointed. <br /><br /><i>“If this were a touching romantic story, in this moment some STRANGE NEW FEELING would wash over Greg, a sense of being understood, in a basic way that he almost never understood. Then, Greg and Rachel would make-out like lovesick badgers. <br />However, this is not a touching romantic story. There is no NEW FEELING that washes over Greg. There is no BADGER MAKE-OUT SESSION.” </i><br /><br /><i>“I can’t believe you’re still reading this. You should smack yourself in the face a couple of times right now, just to complete the outstandingly stupid experience that is this book.”</i><br /><br /><i>“You can take pretty much any sentence in this book and if you read it enough times, you will probably end up committing homicide.” </i><br /><br />See?!<br />No message.<br />Nada.<br />This book doesn’t want you to learn anything!<br />Hurrah.<br /><br />I think the only similarity this book has with a "cancer book" is that you shouldn’t read it in public because seriously, the amount of bellowing laughter this book caused was ridiculous. And kind of embarrassing. My normal, everyday laugh resembles the bark of a dying seal with a cold and this book took that to a whole new level.<br />I’ll let your imagination deal with that one.<br /><br />OK, I’m reading through my review and I’ve realised I’ve not really said anything about this book to convince you whether it’s right for you so I’m just going to stop.<br /><br /><b>This book made me:</b><br />Laugh.<br />Snort.<br />Snort-laugh.<br />Really look forward to see what Mr Andrews writes next. <br /><br /><br /><i>I received an advanced copy of this book from the publishers via Netgalley.</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7165282333334859320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
