<div id="review_256087945" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/256087945" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/256087945?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=debut-author">debut-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=books-for-rainy-days">books-for-rainy-days</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2012">reviewed-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=arc-2012">arc-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer256087945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10458845514782295451"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Me and Earl and the Dying Girl is a very strange book indeed. I’m sure some of you read the blurb and thought: <i>Not another cancer book! Really, are books about teens with cancer the new black?!</i> Yeah, I thought so too. It turns out that this book has very little to do with cancer. It has more to do with several other, completely unrelated things like filmmaking, high school social structure, odd friendships and nagging parents. It’s certainly not a sob story. The only tears I’d shed whil</span>
  <span id="freeText10458845514782295451" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />Me and Earl and the Dying Girl is a very strange book indeed. I’m sure some of you read the blurb and thought: <i>Not another cancer book! Really, are books about teens with cancer the new black?!</i> Yeah, I thought so too. It turns out that this book has very little to do with cancer. It has more to do with several other, completely unrelated things like filmmaking, high school social structure, odd friendships and nagging parents. It’s certainly not a sob story. The only tears I’d shed while reading it were caused by laughter. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>My point is this: This book contains precisely zero Important Life Lessons, or Little-Known Facts About Love, or sappy tear-jerking Moments When We Knew We Had Left Our Childhood Behind For Good or whatever. And, unlike most books in which a girl gets cancer, there are definitely no sugary paradoxical single-sentence-paragraphs that you’re supposed to think are deep because they’re in italics.</i>
</b><br /><br />This is where I would normally write a lengthy plot summary, but I’m afraid my usual reviewing patterns simply won’t work for this book. Greg Gaines is a normal, awkward teenage boy who prides himself in the fact that he doesn’t belong to any of the usual groups in high school, but is on friendly terms with everyone. He only has one real friend, his complete opposite, Earl. When a girl from his school gets leukemia, Greg’s mother makes Greg spend time with her, and as much as he doesn’t want to, he’s too afraid of his mother to say no. <br /><br />Greg Gaines, our main character, assumed the role of the author, which led to a lot of self-deprecating humor (and made me think that he was also, at least partly, an author surrogate). Although I’ll be the first to admit that his observations about his own writing were often hilarious, I did feel that the whole thing was overdone at times. A good joke can only be good for so long before it becomes downright annoying. Here’s just one example:<br /><b>
  <i>And that’s part of the backstory for me and Earl. It’ll probably be relevant later, although who really knows. I can’t believe you’re still reading this. You should smack yourself in the face a couple of times right now, just to complete the outstandingly stupid experience that is this book.</i>
</b><br />That is just one example in which an invisible line was crossed and Greg’s story stopped being funny and became eye-roll inducing. That doesn’t mean, however, that this book didn’t have incredibly funny moments. It is, after all, based almost entirely on humor, and the kind of humor that actually worked for me most of the time. It is what kept me reading even after I realized that there isn’t an actual plot to speak of. The fact that it took me a while to even notice says enough about the kind of narrative we’re dealing with here. <br /><br />I honestly think that I’m not the intended audience for this book, but that didn’t stop me from enjoying it. In many ways, it provides a realistic insight into a teenage boy’s mind, and that’s something we (I) don’t see enough of. Do I think you should read this book? Definitely. It’s not a book that you’ll read compulsively, so it’s best to pick it up when you’re otherwise preoccupied. It’s one of those books you can abandon for a while and go back to whenever you feel like it. There are times when that’s exactly what I’m looking for: a light, fun read that will allow me to focus on other, more important things. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10458845514782295451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer9783866205743429675">"Me and Earl and the Dying Girl" is crude, lewd, silly, heartbreaking, sweet, cynical, honest, and too smart for its own good. Probably one of the funniest YA novels I've had the pleasure of reading. I also recommend watching the movie. Actually, the movie is pretty tame compared to the book (a lot less profanity and sexual directness). Thomas Mann who plays Greg Gaines in the film knocks it out of the park! Holy hell, he's talented. Jesse Andrews is weird little writer (I like weirdoes) who doe</span>
  <span id="freeText9783866205743429675" style="display:none">"Me and Earl and the Dying Girl" is crude, lewd, silly, heartbreaking, sweet, cynical, honest, and too smart for its own good. Probably one of the funniest YA novels I've had the pleasure of reading. I also recommend watching the movie. Actually, the movie is pretty tame compared to the book (a lot less profanity and sexual directness). Thomas Mann who plays Greg Gaines in the film knocks it out of the park! Holy hell, he's talented. Jesse Andrews is weird little writer (I like weirdoes) who does a fine job of balancing humor and heart. Give this offbeat novel a try. Enjoy! </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer749162673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13824648022089453104">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/><b>EDIT: I NEVER change my rating, but this one deserves all 5 and I don't know what assholery I was up to when I first reviewed it and knocked it down half a star. Also, THIS (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.buzzfeed.com/danieldalton/i-know-what-you-said-on-tumblr#.uaV3Y7XmQ'>http://www.buzzfeed.com/danieldalton/...</a>) was a thing a couple of weeks ago and Jesse Andrews already did it for realsies with <i>Earl</i>. Also #2, I used to write non-giffified reviews. How lame.</b><br/><br/>Greg has managed to make it to his senior year by being an acquaintance to </span>
  <span id="freeText13824648022089453104" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br /><br /><b>EDIT: I NEVER change my rating, but this one deserves all 5 and I don't know what assholery I was up to when I first reviewed it and knocked it down half a star. Also, THIS (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.buzzfeed.com/danieldalton/i-know-what-you-said-on-tumblr#.uaV3Y7XmQ">http://www.buzzfeed.com/danieldalton/...</a>) was a thing a couple of weeks ago and Jesse Andrews already did it for realsies with <i>Earl</i>. Also #2, I used to write non-giffified reviews. How lame.</b><br /><br />Greg has managed to make it to his senior year by being an acquaintance to all and a friend to <s>none</s> one. When you’re a rodent-faced, chubby kid growing up in a not-so-great area and attend a high school of cliques that run the gamut of nerd to criminal, it’s probably best to just blend in so you never get singled out. His only friend has always been Earl – a foul-mouthed, chain-smoking, vertically challenged, roundhouse-kicking kid from a broken home, who has pretty much raised himself in a house filled with drug dealing, gangbanging brothers. After Greg decided to give up on having other friends (or ever getting a girl), he and Earl spent all their free time making their own versions of their favorite movies. That is, until Greg’s mother tells him he has to rekindle a friendship with Rachel, a girl from his Hebrew classes ages ago, who is now battling leukemia. Begrudgingly following his mother’s <s>demand</s> request, Greg (and Earl) do as told, eventually letting Rachel in on their secret and sharing their movies with her. Rachel’s dying wish of her new two friends is for them to make a new movie for her. Unfortunately, said movie ends up being the "Worst Film Ever Made" and Greg finds himself in the spotlight he has hidden from all his life.<br /><br />How can I even describe how much I liked this quirky little novel. After realizing he has made the “Worst Film Ever Made”, Greg has taken to paper to write his tale rather than put it on film. His self-deprecation (i.e., “I can’t believe you’re still reading this. You should smack yourself in the face a couple of times right now just to complete the outstandingly stupid experience that is this book”) and complete honesty about being an awkward teenager (“He has just gotten home from school and is trying to read “A Tale of Two Cities” for class, but it is difficult for him to maintain focus, because inside his pants he has AN INEXPLICABLE BONER”) made me have a “you had me at hello moment”. I am always reeled right in by the loveable loser. (And cover art. God am I a cheap date for a good cover.) <br /><br />Although nearly 100% certain I would like this book right from the get-go, I never imagined what would happen when Earl entered my life. Earl is one of my favorite characters of the entire year. He gives you zero time to pity the poverty and drugs he has been raised around – instead he is just a constant ball of hilarity and brilliance and I remain smitten.<br /><br />If you’re concerned about this being a replay of “A Fault In Our Stars” and turning into a huge boo-bag because you’re reading a book that flat out tells you it’s about a dying girl, have no fear. Yes, there is a dying girl, but she is really more of an accessory to the story. Andrews doesn’t let you in Rachel’s life so far as to rip your heart out at her suffering. He just gives you enough info to get you a little misty.<br /><br />If you’re a fan of John Green or Matthew Quick or Stephen Chbosky, you should not be disappointed with Jesse Andrews. I can’t wait for him to write more.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13824648022089453104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16740296352832625221">☺ <b><u>Edit 06/18</u> : The movie looks fantastic! Me want.</b> <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2qfmAllbYC8' rel='nofollow noopener'>Trailer</a><br/><br/>▧ <b>Impromptu reread because <i>what's better than starting vacations laughing?</i></b> ▧<br/><br/><i>This is it</i>. Second time I read it and my opinion didn't change. Yes this is immature at times but what did you expect? <b>The teenagers here feel <i>real</i></b>. Don't wait for the big revelations, for the meaningful things these kids have to say, you'd be disappointed. Don't wait for The Great Romance, either. <b>That's just LIFE and I adored it for its honesty</b>.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>“It's like whe</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText16740296352832625221" style="display:none">☺ <b><u>Edit 06/18</u> : The movie looks fantastic! Me want.</b> <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2qfmAllbYC8" rel="nofollow noopener">Trailer</a><br><br>▧ <b>Impromptu reread because <i>what's better than starting vacations laughing?</i></b> ▧<br><br><i>This is it</i>. Second time I read it and my opinion didn't change. Yes this is immature at times but what did you expect? <b>The teenagers here feel <i>real</i></b>. Don't wait for the big revelations, for the meaningful things these kids have to say, you'd be disappointed. Don't wait for The Great Romance, either. <b>That's just LIFE and I adored it for its honesty</b>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“It's like when a kitten tries to bite something to death. The kitten clearly has the cold-blooded murderous instinct of a predator, but at the same time, it's this cute little kitten, and all you want to do is stuff it in a shoebox and shoot a video of it for grandmas to watch on YouTube.”</b>
</blockquote><br>▒ Original review (December 2014) ▒<br><br><i>I'd been thrown off guard.</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419546850i/13090711._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>To read this book was the best and the <i>worst</i> idea I could have</u> : <br>- Perfect because I couldn't stop laughing.<br>- Not-so-perfect because I couldn't stop laughing <b>in public</b>. <b>Out loud.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419518188i/13086994._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Of course I earned a lot of weird glances. Merry Christmas, that's so nice of you! <br><br>✔ <b>Therefore, I laughed out loud during the whole book</b> : in the train, in the park, in front of my family. Well, the whole time. Mostly, because of <b>Greg</b>, the main character and narrator of the book, the <i>Me</i> of the title, my buddy Greg. <br><br><b>"Music really only interested me as a soundtrack to a movie, and as for sports, I mean, come on. It's some guys throwing some balls around, or trying to knock each other over, and you're supposed to watch them for three hours at a time, and it just sort of seems like a waste. I dunno."</b><br> <br><i><b>Greg</b> was such a <b>relatable</b> character!</i> In my opinion, <b>one of the most credible and believable teenager's voice</b> I've had the opportunity to hear for <i>years</i>. Oh, if you're weird. I was undeniably odd in high-school. Maybe I'm still a bit. So Greg? <u>Here's what I loved about him</u> : <br><br>✔ The <b>highly entertaining movies</b> he makes with his <s>friend</s> <i>coworker</i> <b>Earl</b>. At first, when I became aware that we'd have to go through the description of every single movie they made, I kind of freaked out. I mean, I'm not a movie-<i>hater</i>, but I'm not a movie-<i>lover</i> either. But you know what? It became one of my favorite parts of the book, because those summaries? Awesome. What? You're not taking my word on it? See for yourself! That's free! <br><br><u>
  <b>Astonishing movie #1</b>
</u> : <i>I though the exact same thing!</i><br><br>"<b>Apocalypse Later (dir G. Gaines and E. Jackson, 2007)</b>. <i>Again, not our best title. Once we found out what the apocalypse was, we thought that it was ridiculous that</i> Apocalypse Now <i>was not, in fact, about the End of the World. This movie can best be summed up like this : <br><br>1. Earl, wearing a bandanna and holding a Super Soaker, demands to know when the apocalypse is happening.<br>2. Offscreen, I tell Earl that the apocalypse is not for a while.<br>3. Earl sits in a chair and does a lot of cussing.<br>4. Repeat.</i>"<br><br><u>
  <b>Astonishing movie #2</b>
</u> : <i>Tested and approved by my cats!</i><br><br>"<b>Cat-ablanca (dir G. Gaines and E. Jackson, 2008)</b>. <i>The thing is, cats can't act.</i>"<br><br><u>
  <b>Astonishing movie #3</b>
</u> : <i>Because the title says it all!</i><br><br>"<b>Batman versus Spider-Man (dir G. Gaines and E. Jackson, 2011)</b>. (...) <i>The bat and the spider have never been enemies... until now!!!!</i>"<br><br><u>
  <b>Astonishing movie #3546286</b>
</u> : <i>Ha ha ha, you've seen my point?</i><br><br><s>→ <i>Greg, you're totally cool. I wanna hang-out with youuuuuuuuu.</i></s> Sorry about that.<br><br>✔His hilarious way to relate his own-life and the <b>honesty</b> with which he sees himself : No, Greg isn't perfect, even far from it. He doesn't know how to handle what he sees at first as a burden : that is to say, reacquainting himself with a former <i>not-so-friend</i>, Rachel, <b>because she has been diagnosed with cancer.</b> He isn't popular, isn't selfless, and especially <i>not</i> courageous. But his way to make a one-man-show of his own life was so funny I couldn't help but forgive him, even when he was being a coward. And even if I'm not able to point the <i>exact</i> moment I started to <b>be moved</b> by him, that happened. Suddenly I've been touched by the <b>vulnerability</b> implied by every single sentence we read. <br><br><b>"It was like when a dog makes a human-style face at you and you're temporarily thrown off guard by it. You're like, "Whoa, this dog is feeling a mixture of nostalgic melancholy and proprietary warmth. I was not aware that a dog was capable of an emotion of that complexity."</b><br><br>I've already written more than 500 words and I didn't even begin to deal with the cancer issue. Don't think I'm stalling - I'm not. In my opinion, this book manages to handle the cancer issue in a way so accurate I consider it as a real <i>
  <b>gem</b>
</i>. <br><br><i>Why am I thanking Jess Andrews?</i> <b>Because he never magnifies cancer and cancer patients.</b> You won't find here neither artificially-created love stories nor random teenagers magically answering existential questions. <b>Because cancer <i>does</i> change people, but not always <i>that</i> much.</b> Oh, and Greg is <b>pissed</b>. Yes, he is pissed, mad, and goes through all these emotions which have been labeled as <i>bad</i>. <b>Rachel</b> isn't always fearless and strong : she's upset, scared, she wants to give up sometimes, because fighting all the time is not humanly possible. <br><br>Finally, one of the main character is diagnosed with cancer but can <i>Me, Earl and the dying girl</i> be reduced to it? <b>Definitely not.</b><br><br>That's <i>only</i> an amazing, heart-warming, laugh-out-loud book you don't want to miss. <i>Only</i>. <br><br>Icing on the cake? Listen to Greg : <b>"If after reading this book you come to my home and brutally murder me, I truly do not blame you</b>"<br><br>PS: And I didn't talk about <b>Earl</b>! Earl's the best. That's all you need to know.<br><br><b>"So I said, "Ugh, there was just this badger picture in my head for some reason."<br>It goes without saying that the moment those words left my lips, I wanted to do serious injury to myself.<br>"Badger," Madison repeated. "Like the animal?"<br>"Yeah, you know," I said feebly. Then I added : "Just one of those badger head pictures you sometimes get."</b><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1254687125" />
    <a title="Taylor Knight" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12627819-taylor-knight"><img alt="Taylor Knight" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536879168p2/12627819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1254687125?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taylor Knight" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taylor Knight" href="/user/show/12627819-taylor-knight">Taylor Knight</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1254687125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9792368694798076590">I'd seen so many negative review for this book. My best friend warned me not to read this book and I didn't listen. But I was curious and there was a couple positive reviews so I read it. A small part of me thought I might like this book. Okay, I hoped that I would like this book. But I didn't and I ended up quitting around page 200. I'm not surprised that I didn't like this book (my best friend told me over and over that it was an awful book) but I'm still really disappointed. <br/>I could tell that</span>
  <span id="freeText9792368694798076590" style="display:none">I'd seen so many negative review for this book. My best friend warned me not to read this book and I didn't listen. But I was curious and there was a couple positive reviews so I read it. A small part of me thought I might like this book. Okay, I hoped that I would like this book. But I didn't and I ended up quitting around page 200. I'm not surprised that I didn't like this book (my best friend told me over and over that it was an awful book) but I'm still really disappointed. <br />I could tell that this book was suppose to have a lot of humor in it but it just didn't work for me. I smiled a little bit in the first few pages but it got old real fast. <br />Greg was one of the worst narrators ever. He's right up there with Bella from Twilight and Anastasia Steele from <br />Fifty Shades of Grey. He was so annoying and he just wouldn't get on with the story. It just kept dragging on and on. I don't even know how I made it to page 200.<br />The characters were boring, underdeveloped and not well written at all. <br />I don't understand how an editor could have read this book and thought it was ready to be published. I don't like the concept of this book that much but great writing could have saved it. But I just can't think of anything about this book that I liked other than the cover is kind of cool. <br />I feel like I'm starting to rant so I'm just going to stop here. But overall, I should have listened to my best friend and not read this book because I lost a few hours of my life for nothing and I also wasted $10 on buying this book.<br /><br />My best friend's review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://loganashleyleduc.com/2015/06/26/me-and-earl-and-the-dying-girl-by-jesse-andrews-review/">http://loganashleyleduc.com/2015/06/2...</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1325237114?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1325237114" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1521623067988543350">UPDATE: 1/4/16 I finally saw the movie! Paul, (my husband), and I watched it at home over the week-end. It was equally -(or better) -than the book! Paul kept saying ...."this is so creative"...<br/>We both loved it! <br/>So, if you're not in the mood for the book....I'm sure most people would adore this movie! Wonderful actors! <br/><br/><br/>Fresh frankness, humor, and pathos. <br/><br/>Jesse Andrews writing is outrageous .... funny as hell....that revolves around a <br/>sensitive plot. The dialogue is brutally honest...which is why </span>
  <span id="freeText1521623067988543350" style="display:none">UPDATE: 1/4/16 I finally saw the movie! Paul, (my husband), and I watched it at home over the week-end. It was equally -(or better) -than the book! Paul kept saying ...."this is so creative"...<br />We both loved it! <br />So, if you're not in the mood for the book....I'm sure most people would adore this movie! Wonderful actors! <br /><br /><br />Fresh frankness, humor, and pathos. <br /><br />Jesse Andrews writing is outrageous .... funny as hell....that revolves around a <br />sensitive plot. The dialogue is brutally honest...which is why I must have been laughing <br />most of the entire book. Yeah... I was aware that my heart was breaking at the same time...<br />But good grief... LIFE is GOOD with the type of authentic humor Jesse writes. <br />There is a feeling of 'real' freedom of speech. <br /><br />For a few hours...I was oblivious to all outside noise, and my surroundings. <br /><br />*The movie is playing in our town... I hope to see it before it leaves the small indi <br />theater that it was playing at last weekend. I've already heard fantastic reports. <br /><br />I'd definitely be up for another book with Greg as the protagonist. He is a terrific <br />character. <br /><br />For readers who enjoy Jonathan Tropper - or Shalom Auslander- Jesse Andrews can make <br />you split your sides as much as these other comic-tragic type authors who have been around a little longer. <br />Razor sharp wit.... 'Very talented' young author!! <br /><br />Many congrats to Jesse Andrews!!!! We can use more hilarious books<br />like this in our world! <br /><br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('l9hEbmGrfAdcd+4nNMVfQzn6ZfLcHHg34dNF6RkMBPQ+2Am52DptLkeYahf7Rx2vXAJ07cf8f2UAlJNE+uvBAw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VyCn0qy63Lsdl0OnKcSMpT+/gavYql+xH0YYYZZKUS3+IOoFFSvNkgZ4x5fmRs5JWkeQtMNKWOP+Ac7Mda2U2g==')})
  }
